1 INTRODUCTION
1.1 Purpose
This document describes the requirements on RIS (Remote Installation Service) within the iCAS Program for Upper Airspace.
Some requirements û e.g. the handling of name services or the partitioning of disks û are self-evident and have been implemented in RIS since the beginning. They have been mentioned in early versions of this document, but are removed from newer versions, although they are still persisting. It is intended to produce a future version of this document, which includes an exhaustive list of all requirements on RIS.Other requirements have been specific to particular versions of RIS and particular to the iCAS prototype. These have been removed from newer versions of this document as well.
1.2 Scope
1.2.1 iCAS
The iCAS system is the latest ATS system under development by the DFS which will replace the P1/ATCAS, P2/ATCAS and P1/VAFORIT systems for use in the control of both lower and upper airspace over Germany and the Netherlands.
iCAS is a further development of the existing P1/VAFORIT hosted on new hardware, with a new operating system and a new underlying software architecture. The initial functional capabilities of iCAS shall comply with those of P1/VAFORIT in order to facilitate operational transition at UAC Karlsruhe (iCAS launching Customer) with minimum operational impact.
1.2.2 RIS
Within the iCAS Program RIS provides a way to facilitate the installation and basic configuration of the Linux operating system on a big amount of machines forming an iCAS ATS system.
The operating system is the base for the iCAS application software. As such the requirements for RIS originate partly from the overall iCAS Technical Requirements and partly from development aspects of the application software.
1.3 Documents Structure
The content of this Document is as follows:
CHAPTER 1,ááááááááááááááááprovides purpose, scope and this documentÆs structure.

1.5 Conventions Used
1.5.1 Wording
Will û A "will" indicates requirements that are not testable. A "will" is also used to introduce requirements that are more precisely stated elsewhere.
Shall û A "shall" indicates that the requirement it refers to is mandatory and testable.
1.5.2 Definitions of terms
Explanations shown below are to facilitate the understanding of terms in the context of this document. Only new terms are mentioned.á
The Distribution-Server (disserver) is a Product of the DFS Linux Competence and Service Center. It provides functionality for performing network installations using standard protocols and applications (TFTP, DHCP, NFS). 
The initial load is the procedure of installing and configuring an operating system on a single machine.
The Linux-Plattform is a product created by the Linux Competence and Service Center (LCSC) of the DFS. The Linux-Plattform, or just Plattform for short, abstracts away certain peculiarities of selected Linux distributions. Thus it is possible to replace one distribution by another (e.g. Red Hat Enterprise Linux and Suse Enterprise Linux).
A machine has the role of a RIS Client while it is being installed, configured or maintained by a RIS Server.
Each subsystem within a string has an assigned type. The term "role" is sometimes used, but means the same. The subsystem type or role describes the tasks this subsystem performs.
The Remote Installation Service (RIS) Server is part of a site. It provides functionality to install and configure the operating system on RIS Clients.
A site is a set of iCAS systems sharing some configuration parameters (e.g. ntp server, default gateway, keyboard layout). These systems are meant to communicate with each other using a local area network. A site contains one or more strings.
An iCAS string contains machines of different roles and even with different operating systems installed (e.g. ARTAS). Some roles like iFDPS, iCORRP or iCMD are necessary for running a string. Some roles, like FLS, are not required for all strings. Other roles systems like iSIM do not belong to an operational string. In general a string is a user defined setup of different systems acting as different roles to form a larger system that is used for a special purpose, e.g. for development, test, training or operational use.
Each system has an associated role. This is a name describing the purpose of the system in an iCAS string. The configuration differs among the roles.
A slot is a defined set of partitions on a hard disk. A single slot contains the data of an installed operating system and the application software.

3 FUNCTIONAL REQUIREMENTS
3.1 Common Functional Requirements
This chapter covers the requirements applicable to all roles.
3.1.1 File System
This chapter covers the requirements related to the file system and directory structure.

RIS-REQ-0014 û Default Filesystem Type EXT4BASELinked SRS-Requirements: 97ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On all roles, RIS shall create file systems of type ext4 on all partitions that it defines, except for swap partitions.
#

#

RIS-REQ-0525 û Disserver, DMS, DRF, Install and iTAP-Server RAID Mount PointBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: 138156Related Release: 5.10-01;5.10-02On roles disserver, dms, drf, install and itapserver, RIS shall create a directory:
-á/data on disserver or install,
- /drf_data on drf,
- /icas/backup on dms or itapserver.
#

RIS-REQ-0526 û Disserver, DMS, DRF, Install and iTAP-Server RAID RecognitionBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: 138156Related Release: 5.10-01;5.10-02On roles disserver, dms, drf, install and itapserver, RIS shall automatically mount the RAID to
- /icas/backup on dms or itapserver,
- /drf_data on drf,
- /data on install or disserver,
if an EXT4 filesystem is present and only if the following limits are fulfilled:
- the device is a block device
- the device is not removable
- there is no second device fulfilling the above criteria.
#

RIS-REQ-5036 û Disserver, DMS, DRF, Install and iTAP-Server RAID Mount FlagsBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: 138156Related Release: 5.10-02On roles disserver, dms, drf, install and itapserver, RIS shall mount the partition on the RAID device so that its users can execute applications stored on that device.
#

RIS-REQ-5273 û Disserver, dms, drf, install and itapserver RAID modeNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1576Related Release: 5.10-03On roles dms, disserver, drf, install and itapserver, RIS shall set the ownership of the root directory in the filesystem on the RAID device to:
* user 'dms' and group 'dms' on role dms,
* user 'disserver' and group 'disserver' on role disserver,
* user 'nor' and group 'nor' on roles drf, install and itapserver.
#

3.1.3.1 DFS HW Agent
The following table provides a compact overview about all templates and roles combination for all sites. Each row maps a single template file which source file name is given in the column "Template File" to a single role, which name is in column "Role". The column "Requirement ID" references the requirement specifiying this relationship. The other columns provide some additional information, like applicable sites (coulumn "Sites") and the md5sum of the source template file, column "Template file md5sum". The column "dfshwagent" contains "no" if the role does not get the dfshwagent and other rpms installed. In this case most columns "Sites", "Hardware", "Template file md5sum", and "Template file" remain empty. Otherwise the column "dfshwagent" contains the word "yes" and all other cells in the row are filled.
Source template files are stored in the directory /usr/share/puppet/products/iCAS_PhI/modules/profile/files/icas/dfshwagent/templates/. RIS copies the required source template file to /etc/dfshwagent.conf.template.

RIS-REQ-5227 û Template KRH Empty Known HWNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-995Related Release: 5.10-03On roles atg, epp, fls, isar, itg and smp, RIS shall install on sites ka_isim, ka_lss or ka_opsys the file /etc/dfshwagent.conf.template with md5sum "26d224f2082ccdc328a34925b8ebf68f" and content
'{
áá "sensors": [ ]
}
',
if the machine has the product name is either "Precision 7820 Tower" orá "Precision R7610 Rack".
#
RIS installs and enables the DFS HW Agent on most roles. But it installs the configuration template only on a limited set of hardware. There is the underlying assumption, when a certain combination of role and smbios product name are given, the hardware is of the correct configuration. Otherwise, for unforeseen hardware, RIS does not install a configuration template file. Without this file the startup of the hardware agent service will fail. That means, for example:
* For some roles (e.g. isar, itg, fls, ...) and on Dell Precision 7820 Tower an empty configuration is deployed by RIS. The DFS HW Agent will startup, but cannot provide any data.
* For the roles cmd, fdo, icwp and on the HW, Dell Precision 7920 Rack, no configuration will be deployed. The DFS HW Agent will fail to start.
* For all roles (e.g. isar, itg, icwp, cmd, drf), RIS will not deploy a configuration template file on other HW, e.g. Dell Precision Tower 7810 or Dell PowerEdge R730.

* ( IPv4-Address & Netmask ) | host_identiferThe IPv4-address is the defined network address in dottet-decimal notation for the used device.
* Netmask in dottet-decimal notation as configured for the same device as the IPv4-address.
* "host_identifer" in dottet-decimal notation as configured for the routing configuratoin parameter.
* The operators "&" and "|" perform bitwise AND and bitwise OR of left-hand and right-hand operants.

RIS-REQ-0067 û Filesystem check disabledBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall disable automatic filesystem check for each role at boottime on all partitions.
#
The keyboard layout is configured in different configuration files, because different ôdriversö are used to handle keyboard events. In the console, ækbdÆ is used. In X, æxkbÆ is used. During the installation, the keyboard layout is configured in the anaconda kickstart configuration file. It is also common to provide keyboard configuration parameters via the kernel command line. 
The requirements impose constraints on the keyboard layouts. First, the layouts are defined by means of configuration file settings. Then requirements are defined that will describe the semantics. 
In any case the configuration files:
- /etc/sysconfig/keyboard, 
- /etc/X11/xorg.conf and 
- ks.conf 
are affected. 1. US-Keyboard Layout Definition: 
 o /etc/X11/xorg.conf.d/00-keyboard.conf 
Section "InputClass"
áááááá Identifier "system-keyboard"
áááááá MatchIsKeyboard "on"
áááááá Option "XkbLayout" "us"
áááááá Option "XkbModel" "pc105+inet"
áááááá Option "XkbOptions" "terminate:ctrl_alt_bksp"
EndSectioná o /etc/vconsole.conf 
KEYMAP=us2. German Keyboard Layout Definition: 
 o á/etc/X11/xorg.conf.d/00-keyboard.conf 
Section "InputClass"
áááááá Identifier "system-keyboard"
áááááá MatchIsKeyboard "on"
áááááá Option "XkbLayout" "de"
áááááá Option "XkbModel" "pc105"
áááááá Option "XkbVariant" "nodeadkeys"
áááááá Option "XkbOptions" "terminate:ctrl_alt_bksp"
EndSectioná o á/etc/vconsole.conf 
KEYMAP=de-latin1-nodeadkeysNote: The US-Keyboard Layout is the default keyboard layout.

RIS-REQ-0394 û Default System Local Password Hashing AlgorithmBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01The default password hashing algorithm shall be md5.
#

RIS-REQ-0395 û Configurable Default System Local Passoword Hashing AlgorithmBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall provide a configuration option to allow the user to change the default password hashing algorithm to any of the following:
* md5
* sha256
* sha512
#
For SHA-256 and SHA-512 it would be possible to configure the number of rounds the hash function is iterated. This process is also called "key stretching". Currently, RIS does not provide a configuration parameter to change the number of iterations done by these algorithms when they are configured by the user.

RIS-REQ-0697 û Linux Kernel: THP, NUMABASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On all roles, RIS shall disable
* transparanet huge pages,
* automatic NUMA balancing.
#
THP short story: it might increase latency through allocation of huge pages in a kernel thread and moving memory around in the page fault handler.á
THP Long story:
Each application has its own virtual address space. When a process requests access to data, this data must be loaded into RAM. Since the application only knows the address of the data in the virtual address space, the real address must be calculated. This calculation is supported by the MMU. The AMD64 architecture specifies virtual addresses of 64-bits that can be translated to 52-bit physical addresses. Depending on the implementation of the architecture these addresses might be smaller, for example the Intel Xeon E5-2623v3 CPU support 48-bit virtual addresses mapped into 46-bit physical addresses. If each byte would be addressable, the required computation by the MMU or Software would be overwhelming. Therefore the address space is divided into portions, called pages. The size of page might be 4 KB, 2 MB or even 1 GB.á A 64-bit virtual address contains all the information necessary to translate a virtual to a physical address of a page. Still, the amount of computations requested from the MMU might be extremely high. The TLB supports the MMU in the same way the cache buffers pages from the RAM.
Having a default page size of 4 KB in Linux might result in a lot of processing in the TLB and the MMU. Huge Pages (2 MB) can significantly reduce the pressure on the hardware. A page allocated to a process cannot be assigned to another process. If the process gets assigned a huge 1 GB page, but needs only 1 KB of memory, the remaining memory is wasted. Because a memory efficient use of huge pages might become difficult (set aside at boot time and application must map explicitly) Linux has Transparent Huge Pages (THP). They work through the help of the page fault handler that moves small pages into a huge page and a kernel thread that scans the memory and allocates huge pages in advance. á
Automatic NUMA balancing short story: it might increase latency occasionally by moving memory to CPU and CPU to memory.
Automatic NUMA balancing long story:
The design is to periodically unmap each tasks memory leading to pages faults when process accesses the memory. When a page fault occurs, the page fault handler knows the CPU the task runs on and the node the memory belongs to. If the process's CPU belongs to another node, the page is migrated to the RAM where the task is running. The migration is expensive. Disabling the automatic balancing in the kernel prevents these migrations to happen. This might be advantageous if latency is important as the remote memory accesses are more expensive, but the cost is always the same and always lower than a one-time migration of many pages.á
P-States short story: best ratio of frequency and voltage.
P-States long story:
A P-State is not a C-State! C-States are used to save even more power when the CPU is idle. P-States come into play when the CPU is not idle. The power a CPU consumes mainly depends on the switching of the integrated circuits. This consumed power depends on frequency and quadratically on voltage plus leakage, which can be neglected here. The operating point with the maximum performance is P0. When P-States are enabled in the BIOS, a Linux kernel driver can control the P-States either manually in software or by hinting the desired state to the hardware (HWP), when available. The P-State can be changed several times a second but it can introduce a small latency to switch between P-States.
RIS-REQ-0701 û Linu Kernel: SWAP BehaviourBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On all roles, RIS shall configure the virtual memory subsystem to begin swapping data when RAM is 90% full.

3.2 DISSERVER Requirements
This chapter covers the requirements applicable to the DISSERVER role.á
3.2.1 Installation
This chapter covers the requirements related to the installation of the RIS server.

RIS-REQ-0001 û DVD MediaBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 110ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall be delivered on one or more DVD media. 
#

RIS-REQ-0002 û x86_64 architectureBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 110ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01The first DVD media shall be bootable on an x86_64 architecture.
#

RIS-REQ-0003 û GeneralBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall comprise a software system that allows unattended installation of machines with a Red Hat Linux system via network, where the machines and their installation parameters are registered on a dedicated RIS server. 
#
The purpose of RIS is to provide a way for fast installation of entire sites. A site is a collection of many functionally distinct iCAS Red Hat Linux machines forming the iCAS ATS system and an associated RIS server, where all machines are connected to common IP networks and isolated from other ATS systems. 
As per nature an installation from DVD requires a media and takes a while due to read performance of DVD drives. For this reason the scope of installation for RIS will be as follows: 

RIS-REQ-0004 û Scope of InstallationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01Installation of a dedicated RIS Server within a site shall be done via DVD, and all other machines (RIS Clients) within the site will be installed simultaneously (in batches depending on string definitions) via network from the RIS Server. 
#

RIS-REQ-0005 û Performance RIS ServerBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 123ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01Installation of a RIS Server via DVD shall not take longer than 60 minutes. 
#

RIS-REQ-0006 û Performance 50 clientsBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 124ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01Simultaneous installation of 50 RIS Clients within a site via network (1 GBps) shall not take longer than 60 minutes. 
#
The scope of RIS is to install Linux in pre-defined configurations on pre-defined machines. Especially as the installation procedure will be unattended, the configuration data (name of machine, unique identification of machine like MAC address and / or serial number, IP address, Timezone, root password, à) of machines to be installed by RIS have to be entered manually and saved somewhere prior to the installation procedure. 
By means of these configuration data and by means of unique identification parameters RIS can identify a machine during installation process and can allow installation of known (registered) machines and deny installation of unknown (unregistered) machines. 
The provision of configuration data is under responsibility of site management. The process of making configuration data available to RIS is called registration of a client. 

RIS-REQ-0007 û RIS Adaptation by site managementBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 120ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01Basis for registration of RIS clients within a site shall be configuration files acting as adaptation data source. These files have to contain all necessary configuration data (hostname, IP addresses, routing, NTP servers à) for each RIS client.
#
A tool ris_machine_check will support System-Management with identification of new network profiles. 

RIS-REQ-0008 û Multiple OS slot supportBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 108ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall support installation to multiple slots per machine.
#
Installation in one slot will not affect other slots û unless initialization of all slots is specified.
RIS-REQ-0009 û USB pendrives support for identificationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 118ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall support USB pendrives to determine the target machineÆs identity. With an USB pendrive no more machine specific mapping is necessary on the RIS server. The term USB-Dongle may be used to refer to such a pendrive.
#

RIS-REQ-0010 û GUI to monitor installation statusBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 115ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall provide a HTTP GUI on the RIS Server to monitor network based installations of clients. 
#

#

3.2.2 File System

3.2.8 Tools
This chapter covers requirements related to custom tools available on this role.
3.2.8.1 Sload.sh
The sload.sh utility supports the user by performing an initial load of many RIS client machines in parallel. It does so by checking the state of the clients and the disserver. Finally it reboots the clients, so that they start the RIS installation. Within this section the requirements for sload.sh are defined.

RIS-REQ-0012 û Utility for Initial Load in BatchesBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112, 113ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall provide the command line utility, sload.sh, on the disserver that allows to initiate an Initial Load on a given list of RIS clients. 
#

RIS-REQ-0256 û Parameter to define the slotBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01The sload.sh utility shall provide the parameter '-s' with option '1' or '2' to define whether installation has to be performed to the first or the second slot.
#

RIS-REQ-0257 û Parameter to clear devicesBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01The sload.sh utility shall provide the parameter '-r' to request clearing of all devices on defined client machines during installation.
#

RIS-REQ-0261 û Cleardevices definition in DEFAULT ruleBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01When the user provides the parameter '-r', the sload.sh utility shall add "cleardevices=sda" to the DEFAULT rule of the disserver.
#

RIS-REQ-0262 û Slot definition in DEFAULT rule for -s1BASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01When the user provides the parameter '-s' with option '1', the sload.sh utility shall add "slot=1 ondisk=sda" to the DEFAULT rule of the disserver.
#

RIS-REQ-0263 û Slot definition in DEFAULT rule for -s2BASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01When the user provides the parameter '-s' with option '2', the sload.sh utility shall add "slot=2 ondisk=sda" to the DEFAULT rule of the disserver.
#

RIS-REQ-0471 û Parameter to enable out of band management configurationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01The sload.sh utility shall provide the parameter -b to request configuration of out of band management on all given hosts during installation.
#

RIS-REQ-0472 û Out of Band Management Configuration in DEFAULT rule for parameter -bBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01When the user provides the parameter "-b", the sload.sh utility shall add "icas.ris.obm_configure" to the DEFAULT rule of the disserver.
#

RIS-REQ-0259 û Parameter to define target host machinesBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01The sload.sh utility shall accept a list of hostnames. These names and addresses define the target machines that are to be installed by the disserver.
#

RIS-REQ-0258 û Ping checkBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01Before remote installation is initiated, the sload.sh utility shall ping each host provided in the input list once.
#

RIS-REQ-0260 û Hostname checkBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01Before remote installation is initiated, the sload.sh utility shall check that each hostname provided is defined in the Linux Plattform configuration.
#

RIS-REQ-0264 û SSH connection checkBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01Before remote installation is initiated, the sload.sh utility shall check that ssh connections with pre shared keys to all defined target hosts are supported for user root.
#

RIS-REQ-0266 û Input verificationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01Before remote installation is initiated, the sload.sh utility shall inform the user about the results of the checks and the DEFAULT disserver rule that will be created.
#

RIS-REQ-0267 û Input confirmation requestBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01The sload.sh utility shall ask for user confirmation after displaying the results of the checks or the DEFAULT disserver rule that will be created.
#

RIS-REQ-0268 û Input confirmationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01When asking the user for confirmation, sload.sh shall recognize the <Enter>-Key as user confirmation and all other keys as user abort.
#

RIS-REQ-0265 û RebootBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 112ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01After all checks have passed successfully and the user has confirmed, the sload.sh utility shall initiate a reboot of all defined hosts using a ssh connection.
#

RIS-REQ-5002 û sload dhcp checkBASELinked SRS-Requirements: DerivedITC: 119581Related Release: 5.10-01The sload.sh utility shall check that DHCP is running.
#
3.2.8.2 Image/Rename System
This chapter covers requirements related to the creation and distribution of images containing OS and application SW. The Image System provides an alternative installation mechanism compared to the standard installation procedure using Red Hat anaconda and puppet.

RIS-REQ-0275 û Active Slot Image CreationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 70ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01The image system shall provide functionality to create an image of the "in-use" slot of a previously RIS installed client machine.
#

RIS-REQ-0276 û Inactive Slot Image CreationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 70ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01The image system shall provide functionality to create an image of any not in-use slot of a previously RIS installed client machine.
#

RIS-REQ-0277 û Image Distribution to Existing SlotBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 69ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01The image system shall provide functionality to distribute an image to any existing not in-use slot of a client machine.
#

RIS-REQ-0278 û Image Distribution to Non-Existing SlotBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 69ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01The image system shall provide functionality to create a new slot when the slot does not exist on the target machine and an image has to be distributed.
#

RIS-REQ-0478 û Rename: hostname reconfigurationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 158ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01When performing "rename" of a slot, the hostname shall be set to the new hostname.
#

RIS-REQ-0477 û Rename: Linux Network ReconfigurationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 158ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01When performing "rename" of a slot, the linux network configuration shall become regenerated using the configuration for the new hostname.
#
The intention of the network reconfiguration is to guarantee a successful reboot of the machine to the newly installed slot, so that the ip addresses of all interfaces are correctly setup and connections can be established without further configuration changes.

RIS-REQ-0479 û Rename: Xorg ReconfigurationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 158ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01When performing "rename" of a slot on machines having the role "icwp", the file /etc/X11/xorg.conf shall become regenerated.
#

RIS-REQ-0480 û Rename: SNMP Daemon ReconfigurationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 158ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01When performing "rename" of a slot, RIS shall set the variables "engineID" and "agentAddress" in /etc/snmp/snmpd.conf to the new hostname that resolves to the Software Service LAN IPv4 Address of the machine.
#

RIS-REQ-0484 û Rename: SNMP Trap Daemon ReconfigurationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 158ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01When performing "rename" of a slot, RIS shall set the EngineID for user "cmmcsnmp" to "80001F8804<SWS_HOSTNAME_HEX>".
#
The <SWS_HOSTNAME_HEX> part of the EngineID is the new hostname that resolves to the Software Service LAN IPv4 Address of the machine transformed to its hexadecimal representation. 

RIS-REQ-0481 û Rename: Synergy ReconfigurationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 158ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01When performing "rename" of a slot on a machine having the role "icwp", RIS shall regenerate the configuration file /etc/synergy.conf.
#

RIS-REQ-0482 û Rename: iCAS Software Change_IdentityBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 158ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01When performing "rename" of a slot, RIS shall execute /icas/IS/bin/change_identity.
#

RIS-REQ-0483 û Image Apply: User File RestoreBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 70ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01After an image has been applied successfully to an inactive slot, RIS shall copy all files and directories listed in the file "/etc/icas-restore-file-list" of the active slot from the active slot to the inactive slot.
#

RIS-REQ-0651 û Rename: grub Boot Menu ReconfigurationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 158ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01When performing "rename" of a slot, RIS shall update the grub menu to show the correct title for the inactive slot containing the new image.
#

RIS-REQ-0652 û Image Apply: automatic renameBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 70ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01After an image has been successfully applied to an inactive slot, RIS shall perform "rename" of the applied image using the hostname of the active slot of the target machine.
#

RIS-REQ-0653 û Rename: User ConfirmationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 158ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01When performing "rename", RIS shall ask the user to confirm that the prerequisites
- USB-Dongle is attached,
- iCAS DMN is stopped and
- iCAS Software is stopped
are fulfilled before starting the process.
#

RIS-REQ-0654 û Image System NetworkBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 67ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01The imaging system shall use the iCAS Software Service LAN (SWS LAN) for all operations.
#

RIS-REQ-5032 û Rename: OBM ReconfigurationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01When performing "rename" of a slot, the out of band management configuration, either AMT or IPMI based, shall become regenerated using the configuration for the new hostname.
#
3.2.8.3 Initialise RIS RAID for Images

RIS-REQ-0530 û RIS RAID for Images file systemBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 113ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01The script /root/bin/prepare_raid shall create an EXT4 file system on a disk that has been recognized being usable for disserver images.
#

RIS-REQ-0531 û RIS RAID for Images: script parametersBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 113ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01The script /root/bin/prepare_raid shall support an optional parameter to let the user define the device to be used.
#

RIS-REQ-0529 û RIS RAID for Images: Disk RecognitionBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 113ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01When called without any parameters, the script /root/bin/prepare_raid shall automatically classify a disk as usable for mounting at /data only if the following limits are fulfilled:- size is greater then 2 TiB.
- the device is a block device
- the device is not removable
- there is no second device fulfilling the above criteria.
#

RIS-REQ-0532 û RIS RAID for Images: usage messageBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 113ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01The script /root/bin/prepare_raid shall print a usage message and a description, when called with parameter "-h" or "--help".
#

RIS-REQ-0533 û RIS RAID for Images: user confirmationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 113ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01Before any file system is created on the selected disk, the script shall request the user to confirm this destructive operation by entering the word "yes".
#

RIS-REQ-0608 û Patch-System: GeneralBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 105, 130ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On role disserver, RIS shall provide a Patch-System for creating patches based on media available in the disserver database.

RIS-REQ-0609 û Patch-System: Create PatchesBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 105, 130ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On role disserver, RIS shall provide a Patch-System, that supports changes in
* the config tree,
* in the puppet code and
* in the 3rdParty rpm repository
of a medium. 
#

RIS-REQ-0610 û Patch-System: Create Patches with ChangesBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 105, 130ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On role disserver, RIS shall provide a Patch-System, that only creates a patch if the contents of the supported file-system trees have changed.
#

RIS-REQ-0611 û Patch-System: SelectionBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 105, 130ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On role disserver, RIS shall provide a Patch-System, that supports the selection of a patch for a medium available in the disserver database.

3.2.8.8 DDP

RIS-REQ-5091 û File /usr/local/bin/ddpNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1297Related Release: 5.10-03On role disserver, RIS shall provide the file '/usr/local/bin/ddp' with the owner attribute 'root' and the group attribute 'root' with the access rights user:'rwx', group:'r-x', other:'r-x'.
#

RIS-REQ-5108 û /usr/local/bin/ddp requires between one and 3 parametersNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1297Related Release: 5.10-03The function /usr/local/bin/ddp shall require:
- at least one parameter, otherwise an error message "No parameters given" will be displayed
- and up to three parameters, otherwise an error messageá "Too many parameters. Maximal two patch numbers and a filename.".
#

RIS-REQ-5109 û /usr/local/bin/ddp with one parameterNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1297Related Release: 5.10-03If the function /usr/local/bin/ddp is called with only one paramter, this parameter shall be a disserver patch number to display all the changes introduced with the corresponding patch.
#

RIS-REQ-5110 û /usr/local/bin/ddp with two parametersNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1297Related Release: 5.10-03If the function /usr/local/bin/ddp is called with two paramters, both parameters shall be a disserver patch number to display the differences between the corresponding patches.
#

RIS-REQ-5111 û /usr/local/bin/ddp with three parametersNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1297Related Release: 5.10-03If the function /usr/local/bin/ddp is called with three paramters, it shall display the differences between the patches given as first and second argument for the file given as third argument.
#
3.2.8.9 DFP

RIS-REQ-5189 û File /usr/local/bin/dfpNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1297Related Release: 5.10-03On role disserver, RIS shall provide the file '/usr/local/bin/dfp' with the owner attribute 'root' and the group attribute 'root' with the access rights user:'rwx', group:'r-x', other:'r-x'.
#

RIS-REQ-5112 û /usr/local/bin/dfp shall require a file nameNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1297Related Release: 5.10-03The function /usr/local/bin/dfp shall,
- when a single filename is provided as parameter, show all changes in disserver patches to the specified file,
- when no parameter is provided, show the error message "No parameters given",
- when more than one parameters are provided, show the error message "Too many parameters.".
#

RIS-REQ-5118 û /usr/local/bin/dfp error messageNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1297Related Release: 5.10-03If not exactly one parameter is given to the function /usr/local/bin/dfp, it shall diplay an error message "No parameters given" or "Too many parameters".
#

3.3 iCAS System installation
3.3.1 Common Functional Requirements
This chapter covers the requirements applicable to all iCAS system roles.
3.3.1.1 File System
This chapter covers the requirements related to the file system and directory structure.

RIS-REQ-0174 û PartitionsBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 97ITC: 120890Related Release: 5.10-01On all roles, except disserver, RIS shall create the following partitions for each slot: / 16GB, /tmp 16GB, /home 8GB, /icas 360GB, swap 16GB.
#
3.3.1.2 User/Group Management
This chapter covers the requirements related to the user and group management.
3.3.1.3 Packages
This chapter covers the requirements related to the packages installation

RIS-REQ-0021 û Installation of net-snmpBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On all roles, RIS shall install the following Red Hat packages: 
- net-snmp (>= net-snmp-5.7.2-43.el7.1)

RIS-REQ-0043 û IPV6 deactivatedBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 93, 94, 101ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall disable IPv6 on all machines.
#

RIS-REQ-0044 û Ring buffer for IMAS NICsBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 93, 101ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On all roles, RIS shall set the ring buffer size for IMAS NICs to 4096, if network configuration for iMAS is applied for this host.
#
The Domain Name System (DNS) translates names to numerical IP addresses. It is also possible to retrieve a name for a given IP address. There is one limitation, it is not possible to retrieve for a given name or IP address all other names and IP addresses belonging to the same host. Nevertheless, RIS needs to be able to determine all IP addresses or names of a host. In iCAS, this is realized by the definition of special postfixes. Each name has a postfix identifying the LAN, to which the resolved IP address belongs. 

RIS-REQ-0564 û Ring Buffer "bond2" SlavesBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 93, 101ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On roles fdps and corrp, RIS shall set the ring buffer of all ethernet devices configured as slave devices for bonding device "bond2" to 4096.

3.3.2 Non-Operational Roles Requirements
This chapter covers the requirements applicable to non-operational roles.
3.3.2.1 Install Server Requirements
This chapter covers the requirements applicable to the Install Server role.
3.3.2.1.1 File system
This chapter covers the requirements related to the file system and directory structure.

RIS-REQ-0210 û File capabilities of nmapBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On roles install and smws, RIS shall set file capabilities of nmap to 'cap_net_raw+eip".
#
Machines of class INSTALL are supposed to be equipped with a disk array for data recording purposes. A properly configured disk array is detected as device /dev/sdc by Red Hat. The requirements regarding the automatic configuration are in chapter "Functional Requirements / Common Functions Requirements / Files System".
3.3.2.1.2 User/Group Management
This chapter covers the requirements related to the user and group management.
Installation of the IS RPMs (done by RIS) requires existence of user nor.

RIS-REQ-0074 û Install Server App requires user norBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 89, 91, 105ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On INSTALL role, RIS shall ensure that system local user "nor" is created before Installation of Install Server RPMs. 
#

RIS-REQ-0075 û Permissions of /icas/installBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 105ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On INSTALL role, RIS shall set the ownership of /icas/install to nor:nor and the permissions to 755. 
#
3.3.2.1.3 Packages
This chapter covers the requirements related to the packages installation

RIS-REQ-0076 û Desktop EnvironmentBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01Gnome shall be used as the standard desktop for the role install.
#

RIS-REQ-0078 û Install Server ISDMODLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1512Related Release: 5.10-01;5.10-02;5.10-03RIS shall install Install Server (IS) RPMs version R3.5-03 for the Install Server as described in the release notes of IS.
#

RIS-REQ-0079 û Package amttermBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On role install, RIS shall install package "amtterm".
#

RIS-REQ-0148 û Java web plugin on SMSFBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On role install, RIS shall install ORACLE Java web plugin (java-1.8.0-oracle-plugin).
#

RIS-REQ-0694 û Package ntfs-3gBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 89ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On role install, RIS shall install the RPM ntfs-3g compatible with Red Hat Enterprise Linux 7.8 from the epel repositories.
#
3.3.2.1.4 Network
This chapter covers the requirements related to the network configuration

RIS-REQ-0253 û Variables in icas_netdev.sh for network interfaces on Install ServerBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 101ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall implement the following variables for the role install:
CORE_NETDEV=bond0
MGMT_NETDEV=bond1
#
3.3.2.1.5 Environment Variables
This chapter covers the requirements related to the definition and configuration of environment variables.
3.3.2.1.6 System Configuration
This chapter covers the requirements related to system configuration that are not covered in previous chapters.

RIS-REQ-0553 û Install Server Time To Live (TTL)BASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall provide the configuration parameter "install_server.isd.ttl" to set the Time To Live (TTL) for the Install Server.
#

RIS-REQ-0554 û Install Server TTL ApplicationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On role install, RIS shall apply the value defined of the configuration parameter "install_server.isd.ttl" to the variable "isd_conf" in the file /etc/sysconfig/isd as a startup parameter for the install server daemon.
#
3.3.2.2 SMWS Role Requirements
3.3.2.2.1 File System

RIS-REQ-0577 û File capabilities of nmapBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall set file capabilities of nmap to 'cap_net_raw+eip" on smws role.
#

RIS-REQ-5093 û SMWS PartitionsNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1219Related Release: 5.10-03On role smws, RIS shall create the following partitions for each slot: / 16GB, /tmp 16GB, /home 16GB, /icas 31352 MB, /opt 31352 MB and swap 8GB.
#

RIS-REQ-5190 û directory '/usr/share/gnome-shell/extensions/desktop_stations_gnome_extensions/' for smwsNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1576Related Release: 5.10-03On role smws RIS shall create the directory '/usr/share/gnome-shell/extensions/desktop_stations_gnome_extensions/' with file attributes root:rootá (owner:group) and mode '0755'.
#

RIS-REQ-5196 û Mount NFS shares for smwsNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1576Related Release: 5.10-03On role smws, RIS shall configure NFS client to mount the following NFS shares from disserver:
* <IP_ADDRESS>:/data/users /smusers nfs rw,nosuid 0 0
* <IP_ADDRESS>:/data/smws /data nfs rw,nosuid 0 0
where '<IP_ADDRESS>' has to be replaced by the ip address of the disserver performing the initial load.
#

RIS-REQ-5242 û Directories /data and /smusersNEWLinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: IOPC-1576Related Release: 5.10-03On role smws for sites ka_isim, ka_lss and ka_opsys, RIS shall create the following directories with ownership user:group set to nor:nor: and mode '0755'.
* '/smusers'
* '/data'
#

RIS-REQ-0493 û NTP maxdistanceBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 93, 101ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On all roles, RIS shall configure ntpd to use a synchronization distance threshold (tos maxdist) used by the clock selection algorithm of "3".

RIS-REQ-0226 û Provide /var/lib/AccountsService/users/nor fileBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall provide on iCWP the file /var/lib/AccountsService/users/nor with:
- owner=root, group=root, mode=0644 
- the setting XSession=icwp
- the setting Language=en_US.utf8
- the setting SystemAccount=false
#

RIS-REQ-0227 û Provide files on iCWPBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall provide following files on iCWP:
- /usr/share/xsessions/icwp.desktop
- /home/nor/icwp-session.sh
- /home/nor/.xinitrc
- /etc/udev/rules.d/99-icwp.rules
#
The file icwp.desktop ensures, that the icwp-session.sh gets executed. The icwp.desktop files get loaded by the window manager. icwp-session.sh contains cammands to setup some environment attributes required by iCAS iCWP software.
The file /home/nor/.xinitrc does nothing, but preventing Xorg from launching an xterm during startup.
The udev rules file 99-icwp.rules contains rules for input devices, like keyboard, mouse and touch input devices. These rules guarantee that these devices are correctly configured, even if they are reported in different orders during system boot or at run time (a user could switch the mouse).

RIS-REQ-0112 û Setup of X11 configurationBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: 128104Related Release: 5.10-01The X configuration for iCWPs shall make use of the following screens:
- MDW 
- SDD 
- TID 
- KVM (optional)
#
MDW and SDD share one virtual screen. The TID is configured on a separate screen. The MDW is orientated on the left side of the SDD.

RIS-REQ-0549 û iCWP replace_broadcaster.sh executionBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On role icwp RIS shall provide the user 'nor' with the sudo-rule to execute the script /root/bin/replace_broadcaster.sh as root without password.#

RIS-REQ-0565 û iCWP Kernel: Maximum Number of Message Queue IdentifiersBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On role icwp, RIS shall set the maximum number of message queue identifiers of the kernel to 512.#
The requirement RIS-REQ-0607 is limited to the intel_idle driver, because RIS does not configure the BIOS. It is possible to disable the intel_idle driver and have a Core in a C-State > 1. This is possible, since the kernel uses an acpi driver when the BIOS supports C-States and the intel_idle is configured to not enter C-States. It is not possible to configure the kernel to not use the acpi driver. But after the C-State support is also disabled in the BIOS, the Kernel will stop trying to use them.

RIS-REQ-0656 û X-Server ignores TID Input EventsBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On role icwp, RIS shall configure the X-Server to ignore input events from Touch Input Devices having any of the following names:
* "3M 3M MicroTouch USB controller"
* "eGalaxTouch Virtual Device for Single"
* "eGalax Inc. eGalaxTouch EXC3000-0401-48.00.00"
* "eGalaxTouch P80H84 8084 v230_3_V1 k4.08.165"
#

RIS-REQ-0336 û SNMPD ParametersBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall configure the snmpd to start with the parameters "-LS0-3d -Lf /dev/null -p /var/run/snmpd.pid".
#

RIS-REQ-0337 û SNMPD Configuration: rwcommunityBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall set the snmp configuration parameter rwcommunity to public.
#
The SNMP community string is similar to a password. In Red Hat Enterprise Linux, RIS, the net-SNMP implementation of SNMP is used. Net-SNMP provides three communities ro-community, rw-community and trap-community. The default password for the rw-community (read-write-community) is set to "public" by the requirement above. SNMPv1 and SNMPv2 don't encrypt messages. Passwords are send in clear text.

RIS-REQ-0338 û SNMP Proxy TreeBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall configure net-snmp to act as a proxy for the remote community "public" on localhost port 34000 to map the entire proxy tree to .1.3.6.1.4.1.8173.1.6868.6868.
#
Note: For example, snmp could be configured by adding "proxy -v2c -c public localhost:34000 .1.3.6.1.4.1.8173.1.6868.6868" to the configuratio file snmpd.conf.

3.3.3.3.9.4 Network

RIS-REQ-0380 û Set EPP IPv4 Addresses in /etc/hostsBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 91, 93, 101ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On roles epp and smp, RIS shall map the following hostname lists (one list per line in file /etc/hosts) to the IPv4 address mapped to the corresponding hostname of the role as defined below:
* "papo1 papo-1 sp1 sim" map to the IPv4 address of the peer EPP
* "pcs1 pcs pcs-ss sup" map to the IPv4 address of the peer SMP
#
For example, if the IPv4 address of the EPP/SMP machine is 10.20.52.111, the following two lines are added to /etc/hosts by RIS:
10.20.52.111 papo1 papo-1 sp1 sim
10.20.52.111 pcs1 pcs pcs-ss sup
RIS-REQ-0381 û Peer ATG IPv4 Address to hostname Mapping in /etc/hostsBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On EPP/SMP role,RIS shall map the IPv4 address of a configurable peer ATG host om /etc/hosts to the following hostnames:"gta sim_gta gta1"
#

RIS-REQ-0382 û iSIM Multicast IPv4 Address in /etc/hostsBASELinked SRS-Requirements: derivedITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On EPP/SMP role, RIS shall map a configurable multicast IPv4 address to the following hostname in /etc/hosts:
"allfdds allsps allctrl tower"

* max number of arrays (SEMMNI) = 1024

4 SPECIAL REQUIREMENTS
The requirements listed in this section are subject to removal in later versions, because they are required from the iCAS development / supplier point of view, but not agreed by DFS. 

RIS-REQ-0149 û FirewallBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 91, 101ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01The Linux Firewall (firewalld) shall be disabled temporarily on all machines to facilitate development by Indra. 
#
First investigations of Red Hat 6 and first results of porting the iCAS application to Red Hat 6 by Indra have shown that the startup time of the iCAS application depends significantly on the activation / deactivation of SELinux (Security Enhanced Linux). Having SELinux activated the startup time exceeds certain timeout values so the iCAS application does not start up. For this reason SELinux will be deactivated in the first version of RIS for Redhat 6. 

RIS-REQ-0150 û Disable SELinuxBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 130ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01On all roles, except disserver, RIS shall disable SELinux by setting ôSELINUX=disabledö in file /etc/selinux/config.
#
There is an ongoing discussion regarding "Green IT" namely the possibility to benefit from power scaling facilities provided by hardware and the necessity to disable these facilities in order to achieve maximum performance. For the time being deactivation of the cpuspeed daemon is required. 

RIS-REQ-0151 û Deactivation of cpuspeed daemonBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 91ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall deactivate the cpuspeed daemon.
#
The driver for the graphic cards used in iCAS allows two different clock rates, which are by default set adaptive (PowerMizer). On machines of class iCMD and iFDO it is required to activate the "performance mode" in the nvidia graphical driver, i.e. permanently set the clock rate to maximum. 

RIS-REQ-0152 û Performance mode for graphicsBASELinked SRS-Requirements: 91, 101ITC: Related Release: 5.10-01RIS shall activate the "performance mode" for the nvidia graphical driver on machines of class iCMD and iFDO.
#
5 Appendix A - LAN: PCIe-BUS-Address to device mame mappings
This appendix provides a complete list of configuration data about the exact mappings of ethernet device names to PCIe BUS Addresses. These mappings are important to iCAS as they are statically defined by the customers. If the mappings are not correctly applied by RIS network connections might not be available. The mappings depend on the hardware revisions and configurations as whell as the BIOS and Firmware versions installed on the host machines. Because of this dependencies it is necessary to define the mappings in the specification. Additional HW configuration descriptions are to be found in the "Hardware Configuration User Manual" [2].
Tab. 1:  Table: DFS Device Names Mappings

IDProduct NameRoleComment1iCAS VMware Virtual Platform 3xVMXNET3 + 1xE1000Eallá
Tab. 2:  Table: DFS Ethernet Device Names Mappings

IDeth0eth1eth2eth3eth4eth5eth6eth7eth8eth9eth10eth1110b:00.013:00.01b:00.004:00.0á
